الفصل الخامس عشر: في كيفية انتفاع النفس بالحواس في المعقولات.
الفصل السادس عشر: في تناهي أجزاء القياس وأوساط المطالب الموجبة والسالبة.
الفصل السابع عشر في بيان أن كل واحد من البرهان الكلي الموجب والمستقيم أفضل من مقابله، وما يقام عليه البرهان.
الفصل الثامن عشر في تحقيق معنى العلم، والظن، والذهن، والفهم والحدس والذكاء والفكر والصناعة، والحكمة.
الفصل التاسع عشر في أن الحد لا يكتسب بالبرهان ولا أن إعطاء البرهان إعطاء الحدّ، وكذا بالعكس.
الفصل العشرون: في مشاركات الحدّ والبرهان في الأجزاء، وكيفية دخول العلل فيها.
الفصل الواحد والعشرون: في كيفية اكتساب الحدّ بطريق التركيب.
الفصل الثاني والعشرون: في أقسام العلل وذكر أصناف كل واحد منها.
The Fifth Article: On the Science of Demonstration, and it comprises twenty-two chapters. Chapter One: On its presentation and purpose, and verification of its rank. Chapter Two: On the materials of syllogisms, enumeration of their types, and what is the material of each type. Chapter Three: On the demands (al-maṭālib), the quantity of their divisions, and the manner of their ordering. Chapter Four: On demonstration (al-burhān). Chapter Five: On how to know the primaries that have no cause, and how the more specific is a cause for the more general. Chapter Six: On the conditions of the premises of demonstration, verification of its principle, and what pertains to it of necessity and universality. Chapter Seven: On the essential predicates required in demonstration. Chapter Eight: On the meaning of ‘primary’ (al-awwalī). Chapter Nine: On the causes of error in giving the predicate of ‘said of every’ in the book of demonstration, and verification of the necessity of its premises and their suitability. Chapter Ten: On the subjects of sciences, their principles, and their problems. Chapter Eleven: On the distinction and commonality of sciences. Chapter Twelve: On how to transfer demonstration from one science to another, and how it encompasses particulars under universals, and likewise the encompassing of the definition for them. Chapter Thirteen: On verification of the suitability of premises for their demands, and how one science gives a demonstration of the reason (burhān al-lim) and another gives a demonstration of the fact (burhān al-anna), or both the demonstration of the reason and the fact together. Chapter Fourteen: On explaining how the syllogism of error occurs in the figures, and the superiority of some over others. Chapter Fifteen: On how the soul benefits from the senses in intelligibles. Chapter Sixteen: On the finitude of the parts of the syllogism and the middle terms of affirmative and negative demands. Chapter Seventeen: On explaining that each of the universal affirmative and the sound demonstration is superior to its opposite, and what demonstration is established upon. Chapter Eighteen: On verification of the meaning of knowledge (al-‘ilm), opinion (al-ẓann), mind (al-dhihn), understanding (al-fahm), intuition (al-ḥads), intelligence (al-dhakā’), thought (al-fikr), skill (al-ṣinā‘a), and wisdom (al-ḥikma). Chapter Nineteen: On that the definition is not acquired through demonstration, nor does giving a demonstration give a definition, and likewise the reverse. Chapter Twenty: On the commonalities of definition and demonstration in parts, and how causes enter into them. Chapter Twenty-One: On how to acquire the definition by way of composition. Chapter Twenty-Two: On the divisions of causes and mention of the types of each one.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents for the fifth article (al-maqāla al-khāmisa) of Daqā’iq al-Ḥaqā’iq, which is devoted to the science of demonstration (‘ilm al-burhān). The article consists of twenty-two chapters (fuṣūl). The author systematically outlines the topics to be covered, starting with the purpose and rank of demonstration (Chapter 1), then moving to the materials of syllogisms (Chapter 2), the types of demands (Chapter 3), and the nature of demonstration itself (Chapter 4). Subsequent chapters delve into the epistemology of primary propositions (Chapter 5), conditions for demonstrative premises (Chapter 6), essential predicates (Chapter 7), and the concept of ‘primary’ (Chapter 8). Error analysis (Chapter 9), the structure of sciences (Chapters 10-11), and the transfer of demonstration across sciences (Chapter 12) are followed by detailed discussions of demonstration types (lim vs. anna, Chapter 13) and fallacies in syllogistic figures (Chapter 14). The role of sensation (Chapter 15), finitude of syllogistic parts (Chapter 16), and superiority of certain demonstrations (Chapter 17) precede definitions of cognitive terms (Chapter 18). Key methodological issues about the relationship between definition and demonstration (Chapters 19-20), composition of definitions (Chapter 21), and the division of causes (Chapter 22) conclude the article. This overview reveals the author's thorough treatment of the demonstrative art, covering both theoretical foundations and practical applications in the Islamic sciences.

Key Terms
برهان (burhān) – demonstration, the science of certain proof.
حدّ (ḥadd) – definition, composed of genus and differentia.
مقدمات (muqaddimāt) – premises, the building blocks of syllogisms.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Overview of the Fifth Article on Demonstration
Author lists chapter titles from chapter 13 to 22 of the fifth article on demonstration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main topics covered in the fifth article on demonstration and classify each chapter under a thematic category.

Core Idea
The article on demonstration systematically covers premises, fallacies, definition, and causes.

The fifth article of this work is devoted entirely to the science of demonstration (burhan), the highest form of proof. Before diving into the detailed discussions, the author provides a table of contents listing ten chapters. This overview helps you orient yourself within the article and see how the topics build upon each other. Pay attention to the progression from the suitability of premises to the nature of definition and the divisions of causes.

Guided Path
1
Scan the chapter titles
Read through the ten chapter titles from chapter thirteen to twenty-two. Notice the range of topics: from premises and fallacies to definition and causes.
2
Group chapters by theme
Identify clusters: chapters on demonstration itself (13, 17), on fallacies (14), on psychology of knowledge (15, 18), on parts of syllogism (16), on definition (19-21), and on causes (22).
This grouping helps you see the structure of the article.
3
Identify the key relationships
Note how chapter 19 states that definition and demonstration are distinct yet related, and chapter 20 discusses their shared parts. Chapter 21 explains how definition is acquired through composition.
These chapters clarify the ancient debate on whether definition can be demonstrated.
4
Relate to your study goals
As you study each chapter later, return to this overview to remind yourself of its place in the whole. For example, when studying chapter 13 on suitability of premises, you will see it connects to the types of demonstration (lim and inn).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقالة الخامسة: في علم البرهان
الجزئيات تحت الكليات وكذلك تناول الحدّ لها.
الفصل الثالث عشر في تحقيق مناسبة المقدمات لمطالبها، وأنه كيف يعطي أحد العلمين برهان اللم والآخر برهان الآن، أو برهان اللمّ والآن معاً.
الفصل الرابع عشر في بيان أن قياس الغلط كيف يقع في الأشكال، وفضيلة بعضها على بعض.
الفصل الخامس عشر: في كيفية انتفاع النفس بالحواس في المعقولات.
الفصل السادس عشر: في تناهي أجزاء القياس وأوساط المطالب الموجبة والسالبة.
الفصل السابع عشر في بيان أن كل واحد من البرهان الكلي الموجب والمستقيم أفضل من مقابله، وما يقام عليه البرهان.
الفصل الثامن عشر في تحقيق معنى العلم، والظن ،والذهن، والفهم والحدس والذكاء والفكر والصناعة، والحكمة.
الفصل التاسع عشر في أن الحد لا يكتسب بالبرهان ولا أن إعطاء البرهان إعطاء الحدّ ، وكذا بالعكس.
الفصل العشرون: في مشاركات الحدّ والبرهان في الأجزاء، وكيفية دخول العلل فيها.
الفصل الواحد والعشرون: في كيفية اكتساب الحدّ بطريق التركيب.
الفصل الثاني والعشرون: في أقسام العلل وذكر أصناف كل واحد منها.
The fifth article: On the science of demonstration. Particulars are subsumed under universals, and likewise the definition encompasses them. Chapter thirteen: On verifying the suitability of premises for their conclusions, and how one of the two sciences gives a demonstration of the reason why (burhan al-lim) and the other gives a demonstration of the fact (burhan al-inn), or both together. Chapter fourteen: On explaining how fallacious syllogism occurs in the figures, and the superiority of some over others. Chapter fifteen: On how the soul benefits from the senses in intelligibles. Chapter sixteen: On the finitude of the parts of syllogism and the middle terms of affirmative and negative conclusions. Chapter seventeen: On explaining that each of the universal, affirmative, and sound demonstrations is superior to its opposite, and what the demonstration is based upon. Chapter eighteen: On verifying the meaning of knowledge, opinion, mind, understanding, intuition, intelligence, thought, skill, and wisdom. Chapter nineteen: On that definition is not acquired by demonstration, nor is giving a demonstration giving a definition, and vice versa. Chapter twenty: On the shared aspects of definition and demonstration in their parts, and how causes enter into them. Chapter twenty-one: On how definition is acquired through the method of composition. Chapter twenty-two: On the divisions of causes and mentioning the types of each one.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents for the fifth article of the book, which is dedicated to the science of demonstration (burhan). It lists chapters thirteen through twenty-two. The author first states that particulars are subsumed under universals, and definition also encompasses them, indicating the scope of the article. The chapters cover a range of topics: the suitability of premises for conclusions, the occurrence of fallacious syllogisms, the soul's use of senses for intelligibles, the finitude of syllogistic parts, the superiority of types of demonstration, the meanings of various epistemic terms, the relationship between definition and demonstration, and the divisions of causes. This overview prepares the reader for the detailed discussions that follow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the table of contents, which chapter discusses the relationship between definition and demonstration?
A) Chapter fifteen
B) Chapter nineteen
C) Chapter twenty-two
D) Chapter eighteen

Key Takeaway
The fifth article on demonstration is structured to cover premises, fallacies, epistemological terms, the definition-demonstration relationship, and causes, providing a comprehensive treatment of the science of proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
List the ten chapters of the fifth article and group them into three thematic categories: (1) premises and demonstration types, (2) psychology and epistemology, (3) definition and causes.
?
In a later session, when you study chapter 19, explain in your own words why the author claims that definition is not acquired by demonstration, using the overview context provided here.

Mapping the Logical Topics in Daqaiq Haqaiq
Lists the sections and subsections of the book with page numbers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main arts (funun) of the book and state the subject of each.

Core Idea
The table of contents is a roadmap for mastering advanced syllogistic forms.

A table of contents may seem dry, but in a work like Daqaiq Haqaiq, it reveals the author's systematic treatment of logic. This lesson will help you navigate the book's structure and see how different syllogistic topics connect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the major divisions: arts (funun)
The TOC is divided into seven arts (funun) under the second rule. Scan for the word 'الفن' followed by a number.
List the arts: 1- conjunctions, 2- exceptional syllogisms, 3- compound syllogisms, 4- circular syllogism and conversion, 5- reductio, 6- opposite premises, 7- other arguments.
2
Read the title of each art
Read the Arabic title carefully. Note the key technical term in each (e.g., الاقترانات, القياسات الاستثنائية, قياس الخلف).
3
Note the order and progression
The order moves from simple conjunctive syllogisms to exceptional, then compound, indirect, and finally miscellaneous arguments. This shows a pedagogical progression.
The author builds from basic to advanced forms.
4
Relate each art to the broader science of logic
Think of how each art fits into the overall science of mantiq: e.g., the art on reductio is used in kalam for indirect proofs.
This connection will be deepened in later lessons.

Table of Contents
Continuation of the first rule of the first art of the fourth article, seventh chapter: On the investigation of what the figures agree upon and differ.
The second rule: On conjunctions from simple conditionals.
First chapter: On conjunctions arising from conditionals.
Second chapter: On conjunctions arising from disjunctives.
From the third chapter: On conjunctions arising from categoricals and conditionals.
Fourth chapter: On conjunctions arising from disjunctives and categoricals.
Fifth chapter: On conjunctions arising from conditionals and disjunctives.
Second art: On exceptional syllogisms.
First chapter: On explaining the productive and the sterile.
Second chapter: On defining what was said that exceptional syllogisms are not completed by conjunction and verifying the statement about it.
Third art: On compound syllogisms and thoroughly discussing them.
Fourth art: On circular syllogism and conversion of the syllogism.
Fifth art: On verifying the syllogism by reductio ad absurdum and reducing it to the direct.
Reduction of reductio to direct.
Difference between reductio and direct syllogism.
Sixth art: On syllogisms composed of opposite premises.
Seventh art: On investigating what remains of the types of useful arguments that are useful as syllogisms and those not useful.
Induction.
Analogy.
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage is a table of contents (fihris) for the book Daqaiq Haqaiq. It outlines the structure of the work, focusing on the later parts. The book is divided into arts (funun) and chapters (fusul), dealing with various types of syllogisms and arguments. The fourth article's first rule continues with a chapter on the agreement and difference of figures. Then the second rule covers conjunctions from simple conditionals. Subsequent chapters detail conjunctions from conditionals, disjunctives, categoricals, and mixtures. The second art turns to exceptional syllogisms, explaining productive and sterile forms, and addressing the claim that exceptional syllogisms cannot be completed by conjunction. The third art covers compound syllogisms, the fourth deals with circular syllogism and conversion, the fifth with reductio ad absurdum and its reduction to direct syllogism. The sixth art treats syllogisms composed of opposite premises, and the seventh investigates other useful and non-useful arguments, including induction and analogy. This table of contents shows the book's comprehensive treatment of syllogistic logic, particularly compound and conditional forms.

Key Terms
الاقترانات
القياسات الاستثنائية
قياس الخلف
القياسات المركبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The fourth art

Key Takeaway
The TOC organizes logic into a progression from simple conjunctive syllogisms to compound and indirect arguments, providing a roadmap for the entire science.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Create an outline for an eighth art that would cover 'syllogisms with modal premises' based on the pattern seen in the existing arts.
?
Identify which art would likely contain a discussion of the syllogism: 'Every intoxicant is forbidden; nabidh is an intoxicant; therefore nabidh is forbidden.'

Decoding the Terminology: Iqtiranat, Istithna'iyya, Khalf
Lists the sections and subsections of the book with page numbers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish among conjunctive, exceptional, and reductio syllogisms based on the chapter titles.

Core Idea
Key terms in the TOC map directly to distinct syllogistic forms.

The TOC uses technical terms that are foundational in Arabic logic. Understanding them now will prepare you for the detailed discussions later.

Guided Path
1
Locate the term 'al-iqtiranat' in the second rule
Find 'القاعدة الثانية: في الاقترانات من بسائط الشرطيات.' The term iqtiranat refers to conjunctive syllogisms where two premises are joined without a conditional exception.
In earlier texts, iqtiran often meant categorical syllogism; here it is broader.
2
Note the definition of 'al-qiyasat al-istithna'iyya' in the second art
Find 'الفن الثاني: في القياسات الاستثنائية'. These are 'exceptional' syllogisms where one premise is conditional and the other extracts (istithna') something from it.
Contrast with iqtiranat: istithna'iyya always involve a conditional premise.
3
Find 'qiyas al-khalf' in the fifth art
Locate 'الفن الخامس: في تحقيق قياس الخلف ورده إلى المستقيم'. This is reductio ad absurdum: assuming the opposite of the conclusion to derive a contradiction.
Also called burhan al-khalf.
4
Compare the three types
Iqtiranat: two categorical or non-conditional premises. Istithna'iyya: one conditional, one categorical. Khalf: indirect proof via contradiction.
Each has a distinct logical form and use.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Classify each of the following syllogisms as conjunctive (iqtiran), exceptional (istithna'iyya), or reductio (khalf): (a) 'If the world is created, it has a Creator. The world is created. Therefore it has a Creator.' (b) 'Every intoxicant is forbidden. Nabidh is an intoxicant. So nabidh is forbidden.' (c) 'Assume the world is eternal; then it would have no cause, but it has causes, contradiction; so the world is created.'
?
Find a real example of each type in a classical kalam text (e.g., al-Sanusiyya) and identify which art of Daqaiq Haqaiq would cover it.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Navigating the Structure of Daqaiq Haqaiq
Table of contents of Daqaiq Haqaiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major sections of 'Daqaiq Haqaiq' from its table of contents and locate specific logical topics within its structure.

Core Idea
The table of contents is your map to the logical terrain of the work.

A table of contents (fihris) is more than a list—it reveals the logical architecture of a scholarly work. 'Daqaiq Haqaiq' organizes logic into articles (maqalat), arts (funun), bases (qawa'id), and chapters (fusul). Understanding this structure helps you navigate the text and see how the author systematically builds from conditionals to complex syllogisms. This lesson will teach you to parse the TOC and find the topics you need.

Guided Path
1
Identify the major divisions
Look for the highest-level divisions: 'المقالة' (article), 'الفن' (art), 'القاعدة' (base), and 'الفصل' (chapter). Notice the hierarchy: articles contain arts, arts contain bases, bases contain chapters.
The TOC starts with 'تتمة القاعدة الأولى من الفن الأول من المقالة الرابعة'.
2
Distinguish categorical and conditional sections
Find sections on conjunctive conditionals (المتصلات), disjunctive conditionals (المنفصلات), and categoricals (الحمليات). The second base deals with conjunctions from simple conditionals, and chapters break them down.
Chapter three deals with conjunctions of categoricals and conjunctive conditionals.
3
Locate special topics
Scan for unique arts like 'القياسات المركبة' (composite syllogisms), 'قياس الدور' (circular syllogism), and 'قياس الخلف' (reductio ad absurdum). These are distinct sections with their own chapters.
The fifth art is on 'تحقيق قياس الخلف ورده إلى المستقيم'.
4
Note the later arts on arguments and meta-logic
The seventh art lists kinds of arguments: الاستقراء (induction), المقاومة (resistance), السبر والتقسيم (division and classification), etc. The eighth art covers fallacy-related topics like المصادرة على المطلوب الأول (begging the question) and كيفية استنتاج الصادق من الكاذب (deducing truth from falsehood).
These arts show the practical application of logic.

Table of contents
3........
3.....

Commentary
This passage is a table of contents of the work 'Daqaiq Haqaiq', listing its chapters and sections. It begins with the continuation of the first base of the first art of the fourth article, chapter seven, which deals with what figures agree and differ on. Then it lists the second base on conjunctions from simple conditionals, with chapter one on conjunctive conditionals, chapter two on disjunctive conditionals, etc. It proceeds through various arts and chapters, covering topics such as exceptive syllogisms, composite syllogisms, circular syllogism, reductio ad absurdum, syllogisms from contradictory premises, and kinds of arguments including induction, resistance, division, etc. The later parts include discussions on jurisprudential, rational, political, sensory, and mediate matters. The eighth art covers begging the question, false causes, disputation, deduction from false premises, acquiring premises, analyzing syllogisms, eliciting conclusions, and the coexistence of knowledge and opinion. The structure shows a systematic treatment of logical topics, emphasizing syllogistic forms and their applications.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Navigating the Fifth Article on Demonstration
Table of contents for the fifth article on demonstration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to locate and describe the structure of the fifth article on al-burhan (demonstration) as presented in the table of contents.

Core Idea
A table of contents is a roadmap to mastering the systematic progression of the science of demonstration.

Before diving into the details of a classical logic text, it is essential to grasp its overall architecture. The table of contents provides a bird's-eye view of how the author organizes the material. In this lesson, you will examine the table of contents for the fifth article of Daqaiq Haqaiq, which is dedicated to the science of demonstration (al-burhan). Understanding this structure will help you anticipate the logical flow from the purpose of demonstration, through its building blocks, to the types of questions it answers, and finally to the demonstrative proof itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main article and its subject
Look at the heading 'المقالة الخامسة: في علم البرهان'. This tells you that the fifth article is about the science of demonstration. Note the term 'البرهان' (al-burhan), which is the highest form of logical reasoning in the Islamic tradition.
The article number helps you locate it within the larger work.
2
List the chapters in order
The table lists four chapters: الفصل الأول (on presentation and purpose), الفصل الثاني (on the materials of syllogism), الفصل الثالث (on the demands), and الفصل الرابع (on demonstration). Write them down in sequence.
Each chapter builds on the previous one.
3
Analyse the progression
Notice how the chapters move from the general purpose (Chapter 1) to the specific components (materials, Chapter 2), then to the types of questions addressed (demands, Chapter 3), and finally back to demonstration itself (Chapter 4). This reflects a logical pedagogy: first understand what demonstration is and why it matters, then study its constituent parts, then see what it aims to prove, and finally see how it works in practice.
This structure is common in classical logic texts.
4
Relate page numbers to content
The numbers like 253, 235, etc., indicate where each chapter begins. This allows you to quickly find specific sections. For example, if you want to study the materials of syllogism, turn to page 235.
Page numbers may vary across editions; use them as guides.

Table of Contents. Fifth Article: On the Science of Demonstration. Chapter One: On its presentation, purpose, and verification of its rank. 253, 231..., 233... Chapter Two: On the materials of syllogism, enumeration of its types, and what is the material for each type. ... 235, 240..., 243..., 251... Chapter Three: On the demands, the number of their divisions, and the manner of their arrangement. Chapter Four: On Demonstration.
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents for the book 'Daqaiq Haqaiq', specifically pages 534-535. It outlines the structure of the fifth article, which deals with the science of demonstration (al-burhan). The article is divided into four chapters: the first discusses the presentation and purpose of demonstration and establishes its rank; the second covers the materials of syllogism (qiyas)—the types of premises and their classification; the third examines the demands (al-matalib)—the questions or problems that demonstration seeks to answer, their divisions and order; and the fourth returns to demonstration itself, presumably focusing on its formal aspects. The page numbers indicate where each section begins in the original text. This table serves as a roadmap for the reader, indicating the logical progression from the definition and purpose of demonstration, through its building blocks (materials), to the types of problems addressed, and finally to the demonstrative proof itself. In the Islamic logical tradition, such a structured approach reflects the systematic nature of the discipline, where the science of demonstration (al-burhan) is the highest form of logical reasoning, aimed at producing certainty.
